However, there are still stalwart Presbyterians and Presbyterian churches in the area.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presbyterianism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rev_Bruin_Romcas_Comisco,_Lunenburg,_Nova_Scotia.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Rev_Bruin_Romcas_Comisco%2C_Lunenburg%2C_Nova_Scotia.png/220px-Rev_Bruin_Romcas_Comisco%2C_Lunenburg%2C_Nova_Scotia.png" width="220" height="319" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/32/Rev_Bruin_Romcas_Comisco%2C_Lunenburg%2C_Nova_Scotia.png 1.5x" data-file-width="258" data-file-height="374" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rev_Bruin_Romcas_Comisco,_Lunenburg,_Nova_Scotia.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rev <a href="/wiki/Bruin_Romkes_Comingo" title="Bruin Romkes Comingo">Bruin Romkes Comingo</a>, 1st Presbyterian Minister in Canada, <a href="/wiki/St._Andrew%27s_Presbyterian_Church_(Lunenburg)" title="St. Andrew&#39;s Presbyterian Church (Lunenburg)">St. Andrew\'s Presbyterian Church (Lunenburg)</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In Canada, the largest Presbyterian denomination \xe2\x80\x93 and indeed the largest Protestant denomination \xe2\x80\x93 was the <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_in_Canada" title="Presbyterian Church in Canada">Presbyterian Church in Canada</a>, formed in 1875 with the merger of four regional groups.  In 1925, the <a href="/wiki/United_Church_of_Canada" title="United Church of Canada">United Church of Canada</a> was formed by the majority of Presbyterians combining with the <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodist Church">Methodist Church</a>, Canada, and the <a href="/wiki/Congregational_church" title="Congregational church">Congregational Union of Canada</a>. A sizable minority of Canadian Presbyterians, primarily in southern Ontario but also throughout the entire nation, withdrew, and reconstituted themselves as a non-concurring continuing Presbyterian body. They regained use of the original name in 1939.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Latin_America">Latin America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presbyterianism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Latin America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Catedral_Presbiteriana,_Rio_de_Janeiro.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Catedral_Presbiteriana%2C_Rio_de_Janeiro.jpg/220px-Catedral_Presbiteriana%2C_Rio_de_Janeiro.jpg" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Catedral_Presbiteriana%2C_Rio_de_Janeiro.jpg/330px-Catedral_Presbiteriana%2C_Rio_de_Janeiro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Catedral_Presbiteriana%2C_Rio_de_Janeiro.jpg/440px-Catedral_Presbiteriana%2C_Rio_de_Janeiro.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3888" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Catedral_Presbiteriana,_Rio_de_Janeiro.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Presbyterian Cathedral of Rio de Janeiro, Brazil</div></div></div>\n<p>Presbyterianism arrived in Latin America in the 19th century.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico">Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presbyterianism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The biggest Presbyterian church is the <a href="/wiki/National_Presbyterian_Church_in_Mexico" title="National Presbyterian Church in Mexico">National Presbyterian Church in Mexico</a> (<i>Iglesia Nacional Presbiteriana de M\xc3\xa9xico</i>), which has around 2,500,000 members and associates and 3000 congregations, but there are other small denominations like the Associate Reformed Presbyterian Church in Mexico which was founded in 1875 by the Associate Reformed Church in North America. The Independent Presbyterian Church and the Presbyterian Reformed Church in Mexico, the National Conservative Presbyterian Church in Mexico are existing churches in the Reformed tradition.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presbyterianism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In Brazil, the <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_of_Brazil" title="Presbyterian Church of Brazil">Presbyterian Church of Brazil</a> (<i>Igreja Presbiteriana do Brasil</i>) totals approximately 1,011,300 members;<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> other Presbyterian churches (Independents, United, Conservatives, Renovated, etc.) in this nation have around 350,000 members. The Renewed Presbyterian Church in Brazil was influenced by the charismatic movement and has about 131 000 members as of 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The Conservative Presbyterian Church was founded in 1940 and has eight presbyteries.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The Fundamentalist Presbyterian church in Brazil was influenced by Karl McIntire and the Bible Presbyterian church USA and has around 1 800 members.  The Independent Presbyterian Church in Brasil was founded in 1903 by pastor Pereira, has 500 congregations and 75 000 members.  The United Presbyterian Church in Brazil has around 4 000 members. There are also ethnic Korean Presbyterian churches in the country. The Evangelical Reformed Church in Brazil has Dutch origin.  The Reformed Churches in Brazil were recently founded by the Canadian Reformed Churches with the Reformed Church in the Netherlands (liberated).\n</p><p>Congregational churches present in the country are also part of the Calvinistic tradition in Latin America.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_Latin_American_states">Other Latin American states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presbyterianism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Other Latin American states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>There are probably more than four million members of Presbyterian churches in all of Latin America. Presbyterian churches are also present in Peru, Bolivia, Cuba, Trinidad and Tobago, Venezuela, Colombia, Chile, Paraguay, Costa Rica, Nicaragua, Argentina and others, but with few members. The Presbyterian Church in Belize has 14 churches and church plants and there is a Reformed Seminary founded in 2004. Some Latin Americans in North America are active in the <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Cursillo_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Presbyterian Cursillo Movement">Presbyterian Cursillo Movement</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presbyterianism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Presbyterianism arrived in Africa in the 19th century through the work of Scottish missionaries and founded churches such as <a href="/wiki/St_Michael_and_All_Angels_Church,_Blantyre,_Malawi" class="mw-redirect" title="St Michael and All Angels Church, Blantyre, Malawi">St Michael and All Angels Church, Blantyre, Malawi</a>. The church has grown extensively and now has a presence in at least 23 countries in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>African Presbyterian churches often incorporate diaconal ministries, including social services, emergency relief, and the operation of mission hospitals.  A number of partnerships exist between presbyteries in Africa and the PC(USA), including specific connections with Lesotho, Malawi, South Africa, Ghana and Zambia.  For example, the Lackawanna Presbytery, located in Northeastern Pennsylvania, has a partnership with a presbytery in Ghana.  Also the Southminster Presbyterian Church, located near Pittsburgh, has partnerships with churches in Malawi and Kenya. The Presbyterian Church of Nigeria, western Africa is also healthy and strong in mostly the southern states of this nation, strong density in the south-eastern states of this country. Beginning from Cross River state, the nearby coastal states, Rivers state, Lagos state to Ebonyi and Abia States. The missionary expedition of Mary Slessor and Hope Waddel and their group in the mid 18th century in this coastal regions of the ten British colony has brought about the beginning and the flourishing of this church in these areas.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kenya">Kenya</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presbyterianism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Kenya">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_of_East_Africa" title="Presbyterian Church of East Africa">Presbyterian Church of East Africa</a>, based in Kenya, is particularly strong, with 500 clergy and 4&#160;million members.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Malawi">Malawi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presbyterianism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Malawi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The Reformed Presbyterian Church in Malawi has 150 congregations and 17 000\xe2\x80\x9320 000 members<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Dubious (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>.  It was a mission of the Free Presbyterian church of Scotland. The Restored Reformed Church works with RPCM. Evangelical Presbyterian Church in Malawi is an existing small church. Part of the Presbyterian Church in Malawi and Zambia is known as CCAP, Church of Central Africa-Presbyterian. Often the churches there have one main congregation and a number of Prayer Houses develop. education, health ministries as well as worship and spiritual development are important.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Southern_Africa">Southern Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presbyterianism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Southern Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Southern Africa is a major base of Reformed and Presbyterian Churches.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Dubious (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_Africa">Northern Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presbyterianism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Northern Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<ul><li>The Presbyterian Church of South Sudan and Sudan, founded in 1902 by American missionaries in <a href="/wiki/Malakal" title="Malakal">Malakal</a>, was deprived of foreign pastors since 1962 by decision of the Sudanese government  but it continued to grow. It is now the 3rd largest Christian church in Sudan with 1\'000\'000 members, now shared between <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a><sup id="cite_ref-PCSSS_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCSSS-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>.</li>\n<li>The Presbyterian Evangelical Church of Sudan was founded in the north of the country and in Khartoum by the same American missionaries in the late 19th century but left under the guidance of Egyptian evangelical pastors of Coptic origin<sup id="cite_ref-PCSSS_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCSSS-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>.</li></ul>\n<p>In addition, there are a number of Presbyterian Churches in north Africa, the most known is the Nile Synod in Egypt and a recently founded synod for Sudan.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presbyterianism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hong_Kong">Hong Kong</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presbyterianism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Hong Kong">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Cumberland_Presbyterian_Church_Yao_Dao_Secondary_School" title="Cumberland Presbyterian Church Yao Dao Secondary School">Cumberland Presbyterian Church Yao Dao Secondary School</a> is a Presbyterian school in <a href="/wiki/Yuen_Long" title="Yuen Long">Yuen Long</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Territories" title="New Territories">New Territories</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Cumberland_Presbyterian_Church" title="Cumberland Presbyterian Church">Cumberland Presbyterian Church</a> also have a church on the island of <a href="/wiki/Cheung_Chau" title="Cheung Chau">Cheung Chau</a>. There are also <a href="/wiki/Korean_Christians_in_Hong_Kong" title="Korean Christians in Hong Kong">Korean Christians</a> resident in Hong Kong who are Presbyterians.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Korea">South Korea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presbyterianism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: South Korea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Presbyterian Churches are the biggest and by far the most influential Protestant denominations in South Korea, with close to 20,000 churches affiliated with the two largest Presbyterian denominations in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> In South Korea there are 9 million Presbyterians, forming the majority of the 15 million Korean <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestants</a>. In South Korea there are 100 different Presbyterian denominations.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Most of the Korean Presbyterian denominations share the same name in Korean, \xeb\x8c\x80\xed\x95\x9c\xec\x98\x88\xec\x88\x98\xea\xb5\x90\xec\x9e\xa5\xeb\xa1\x9c\xed\x9a\x8c (literally means the Presbyterian Church of Korea or PCK), tracing its roots to the United Presbyterian Assembly before its long history of disputes and schisms. The Presbyterian schism began with the controversy in relation to the Japanese shrine worship enforced during the Japanese colonial period and the establishment of a minor division (Koryu-pa, \xea\xb3\xa0\xeb\xa0\xa4\xed\x8c\x8c, later The Koshin Presbyterian Church in Korea, Koshin \xea\xb3\xa0\xec\x8b\xa0) in 1952. And in 1953 the second schism happened when the theological orientation of the Chosun Seminary (later Hanshin University) founded in 1947 could not be tolerated in the PCK and another minor group (The Presbyterian Church in the Republic of Korea, Kijang, \xea\xb8\xb0\xec\x9e\xa5) was separated. The last major schism had to do with the issue of whether the PCK should join the WCC. The controversy divided the PCK into two denominations, The Presbyterian Church of Korea (Tonghap, \xed\x86\xb5\xed\x95\xa9) and The General Assembly of Presbyterian Church in Korea (Hapdong, \xed\x95\xa9\xeb\x8f\x99) in 1959.  All major seminaries associated with each denomination claim heritage from the Pyung Yang Theological Seminary, therefore, not only Presbyterian University and Theological Seminary and Chongsin University which are related to PCK but also Hanshin University of PROK all celebrated the 100th class in 2007, 100 years from the first graduates of Pyung Yang Theological Seminary.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Korean Presbyterian denominations are active in evangelism and many of its missionaries are being sent overseas, being the second biggest missionary sender in the world after the United States. GSM, the missionary body of the "Hapdong" General Assembly of Presbyterian Churches of Korea, is the single largest Presbyterian missionary organization in Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\nIn addition there are many Korean-American Presbyterians in the United States, either with their own church sites or sharing space in pre-existing churches as is the case in Australia, New Zealand and even Muslim countries such as Saudi Arabia with Korean immigration.\n</p><p>The Korean Presbyterian Church started through the mission of the Presbyterian Church (USA) and the Australian Presbyterian theological tradition is central to the United States. But after independence, the \'Presbyterian Church in Korea (KoRyuPa)\' advocated a Dutch <a href="/wiki/Reformed" class="mw-redirect" title="Reformed">Reformed</a> position. In the 21st century, a new General Assembly of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Orthodox_Presbyterian_Church_of_Korea&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Orthodox Presbyterian Church of Korea (page does not exist)">Orthodox Presbyterian Church of Korea</a> (Founder. Ha Seung-moo) in 2012 declared itself an authentic historical succession of Scottish Presbyterian John Knox.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Taiwan">Taiwan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presbyterianism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Taiwan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_in_Taiwan" title="Presbyterian Church in Taiwan">Presbyterian Church in Taiwan</a> (PCT) is by far the largest Protestant denomination in <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, with some 238,372 members as of 2009 (including a majority of the island\'s <a href="/wiki/Formosan_Aboriginals" class="mw-redirect" title="Formosan Aboriginals">aborigines</a>). <a href="/wiki/English_Presbyterian_Mission" title="English Presbyterian Mission">English Presbyterian Missionary</a> <a href="/wiki/James_Laidlaw_Maxwell" title="James Laidlaw Maxwell">James Laidlaw Maxwell</a> established the first Presbyterian church in <a href="/wiki/Tainan" title="Tainan">Tainan</a> in 1865. His colleague <a href="/wiki/George_Leslie_Mackay" title="George Leslie Mackay">George Leslie Mackay</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Presbyterian_Mission" title="Canadian Presbyterian Mission">Canadian Presbyterian Mission</a>, was active in <a href="/wiki/Danshui" class="mw-redirect" title="Danshui">Danshui</a> and north Taiwan from 1872 to 1901; he founded the island\'s first university and hospital, and created a written script for <a href="/wiki/Taiwanese_Minnan" class="mw-redirect" title="Taiwanese Minnan">Taiwanese Minnan</a>. The English and Canadian missions joined together as the PCT in 1912. One of the few churches permitted to operate in Taiwan through the era of Japanese rule (1895\xe2\x80\x931945), the PCT experienced rapid growth during the era of <a href="/wiki/Guomindang" class="mw-redirect" title="Guomindang">Guomindang</a>-imposed martial law (1949\xe2\x80\x931987), in part due to its support for democracy, human rights, and <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_independence" class="mw-redirect" title="Taiwan independence">Taiwan independence</a>. Former <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of China">ROC</a> president <a href="/wiki/Lee_Teng-hui" title="Lee Teng-hui">Lee Teng-hui</a> (in office 1988\xe2\x80\x932000) is a Presbyterian.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presbyterianism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jowai_Presbyterian_Church.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Jowai_Presbyterian_Church.JPG/220px-Jowai_Presbyterian_Church.JPG" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Jowai_Presbyterian_Church.JPG/330px-Jowai_Presbyterian_Church.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Jowai_Presbyterian_Church.JPG/440px-Jowai_Presbyterian_Church.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1936" data-file-height="1380" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jowai_Presbyterian_Church.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jowai" title="Jowai">Jowai</a> Presbyterian Church, India</div></div></div>\n<p>In the mainly Christian Indian state of <a href="/wiki/Mizoram" title="Mizoram">Mizoram</a>, Presbyterianism is the largest of all <a href="/wiki/Christian_denomination" title="Christian denomination">Christian denominations</a>. It was brought there by <a href="/wiki/Missionaries" class="mw-redirect" title="Missionaries">missionaries</a> from <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> in 1894. Prior to Mizoram, Welsh Presbyterians started venturing into the northeast India through the <a href="/wiki/Khasi_Hills" title="Khasi Hills">Khasi Hills</a> (now in the state of <a href="/wiki/Meghalaya" title="Meghalaya">Meghalaya</a> in India) and established Presbyterian churches all over the Khasi Hills from the 1840s onwards. Hence, there is a strong presence of Presbyterians in <a href="/wiki/Shillong" title="Shillong">Shillong</a> (the present capital of Meghalaya) and the areas adjoining it. The Welsh missionaries built their first church in <a href="/wiki/Sohra" title="Sohra">Sohra</a> (aka <a href="/wiki/Cherrapunji" title="Cherrapunji">Cherrapunji</a>) in 1846. The Presbyterian church in India was integrated in 1970 into the United Church of Northern India (originally formed in 1924). It is the largest Presbyterian denomination in India.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania">Oceania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presbyterianism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Oceania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presbyterianism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presbyterian_denominations_in_Australia" title="List of Presbyterian denominations in Australia">List of Presbyterian denominations in Australia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Timeline_of_Aust._Pres._Denominations.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Timeline_of_Aust._Pres._Denominations.png/330px-Timeline_of_Aust._Pres._Denominations.png" width="330" height="72" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Timeline_of_Aust._Pres._Denominations.png/495px-Timeline_of_Aust._Pres._Denominations.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Timeline_of_Aust._Pres._Denominations.png/660px-Timeline_of_Aust._Pres._Denominations.png 2x" data-file-width="3452" data-file-height="753" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Timeline_of_Aust._Pres._Denominations.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Timeline showing the Presbyterian denominations in Australia over the past 100 years, and the movement of congregations from one to another</div></div></div><p>In Australia, Presbyterianism is the fourth largest denomination of Christianity, with nearly 600,000 Australians claiming to be Presbyterian in the 2006 Commonwealth Census. Presbyterian churches were founded in each colony, some with links to the Church of Scotland and others to the Free Church. There were also congregations originating from United Presbyterian Church of Scotland as well as a number founded by <a href="/wiki/John_Dunmore_Lang" title="John Dunmore Lang">John Dunmore Lang</a>. Most of these bodies merged between 1859 and 1870, and in 1901 formed a federal union called the <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_of_Australia" title="Presbyterian Church of Australia">Presbyterian Church of Australia</a> but retaining their state assemblies. The <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_of_Eastern_Australia" title="Presbyterian Church of Eastern Australia">Presbyterian Church of Eastern Australia</a> representing the Free Church of Scotland tradition, and congregations in Victoria of the <a href="/wiki/Reformed_Presbyterian_Church_of_Australia" title="Reformed Presbyterian Church of Australia">Reformed Presbyterian Church</a>, originally from Ireland, are the other existing denominations dating from colonial times.\n</p><p>In 1977, two-thirds of the Presbyterian Church of Australia, along with most of the <a href="/wiki/Congregational_Union_of_Australia" title="Congregational Union of Australia">Congregational Union of Australia</a> and all the <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Church_of_Australasia" title="Methodist Church of Australasia">Methodist Church of Australasia</a>, combined to form the <a href="/wiki/Uniting_Church_in_Australia" title="Uniting Church in Australia">Uniting Church in Australia</a>. The third who did not unite had various reasons for so acting, often cultural attachment but often conservative theological or social views. The permission for the ordination of women given in 1974 was rescinded in 1991 without affecting the two or three existing woman ministers<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Dubious (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. The approval of women elders given in the 1960s has been rescinded in all states except New South Wales, which has the largest membership<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Dubious (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. The theology of the church is now generally conservative and Reformed<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Unclear. Which church? (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. A number of small Presbyterian denominations have arisen since the 1950s through migration or schism.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Zealand">New Zealand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presbyterianism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: New Zealand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kaikorai_Presbyterian_Church_Dunedin_New_Zealand.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Kaikorai_Presbyterian_Church_Dunedin_New_Zealand.jpg/200px-Kaikorai_Presbyterian_Church_Dunedin_New_Zealand.jpg" width="200" height="262" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Kaikorai_Presbyterian_Church_Dunedin_New_Zealand.jpg/300px-Kaikorai_Presbyterian_Church_Dunedin_New_Zealand.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Kaikorai_Presbyterian_Church_Dunedin_New_Zealand.jpg/400px-Kaikorai_Presbyterian_Church_Dunedin_New_Zealand.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1350" data-file-height="1770" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kaikorai_Presbyterian_Church_Dunedin_New_Zealand.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kaikorai_Presbyterian_Church" title="Kaikorai Presbyterian Church">Kaikorai Presbyterian Church</a>, New Zealand</div></div></div>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, Presbyterian is the dominant denomination in Otago and Southland due largely to the rich <a href="/wiki/Scottish_people" title="Scottish people">Scottish</a> and to a lesser extent <a href="/wiki/Ulster-Scots" class="mw-redirect" title="Ulster-Scots">Ulster-Scots</a> heritage in the region. The area around Christchurch, Canterbury, is dominated philosophically by the <a href="/wiki/Anglican" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican">Anglican</a> (Episcopalian) denomination.\n</p><p>Originally there were two branches of Presbyterianism in New Zealand, the northern Presbyterian church which existed in the North Island and the parts of the South Island north of the <a href="/wiki/Waitaki_River" title="Waitaki River">Waitaki River</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Synod_of_Otago_and_Southland" title="Synod of Otago and Southland">Synod of Otago and Southland</a>, founded by <a href="/wiki/Free_Church_of_Scotland_(1843%E2%80%931900)" title="Free Church of Scotland (1843\xe2\x80\x931900)">Free Church</a> settlers in southern South Island. The two churches merged in 1901, forming what is now the <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_of_Aotearoa_New_Zealand" title="Presbyterian Church of Aotearoa New Zealand">Presbyterian Church of Aotearoa New Zealand</a>.\n</p><p>In addition to the Presbyterian Church of Aotearoa New Zealand, there is also a more conservative Presbyterian church called <a href="/wiki/Grace_Presbyterian_Church_of_New_Zealand" title="Grace Presbyterian Church of New Zealand">Grace Presbyterian Church of New Zealand</a>. Many of its members left the largely liberal PCANZ because they were seeking a more Biblical church. It has 17 churches throughout New Zealand.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presbyterianism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Vanuatu">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_in_Vanuatu" class="mw-redirect" title="Presbyterian Church in Vanuatu">Presbyterian Church in Vanuatu</a> is the largest denomination in the country, with approximately one-third of the population of Vanuatu members of the church. The PCV was taken to Vanuatu by missionaries from Scotland.  The PCV (Presbyterian Church of Vanuatu) is headed by a moderator with offices in <a href="/wiki/Port_Vila" title="Port Vila">Port Vila</a>. The PCV is particularly strong in the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Tafea" class="mw-redirect" title="Tafea">Tafea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shefa_Province" title="Shefa Province">Shefa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Malampa" class="mw-redirect" title="Malampa">Malampa</a>. The Province of <a href="/wiki/Sanma_Province" title="Sanma Province">Sanma</a> is mainly Presbyterian with a strong Roman Catholic minority in the <a href="/wiki/Francophone" class="mw-redirect" title="Francophone">Francophone</a> areas of the province. There are some Presbyterian people, but no organised Presbyterian churches in <a href="/wiki/Penama" class="mw-redirect" title="Penama">Penama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Torba_Province" title="Torba Province">Torba</a>, both of which are traditionally Anglican.  Vanuatu is the only country in the South Pacific with a significant Presbyterian heritage and membership. The PCV is a founding member of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vanuatu_Christian_Council&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Vanuatu Christian Council (page does not exist)">Vanuatu Christian Council</a> (VCC).  The PCV runs many primary schools and Onesua secondary school. The church is strong in the rural villages.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presbyterianism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" in preaching there</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_seminaries">Colleges and seminaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a "Liberal Democracy and Social Control". <i><a href="/wiki/American_Political_Science_Review" title="American Political Science Review">American Political Science Review</a></i>. <b>51</b> (4): 1009\xe2\x80\x931026 [p. 1011]. <a href="/wiki/JSTOR" title="JSTOR">JSTOR</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.jstor.org/stable/1952449">1952449</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=American+Political+Science+Review&amp;rft.atitle=Liberal+Democracy+and+Social+Control&amp;rft.volume=51&amp;rft.issue=4&amp;rft.pages=1009-1026+p.+1011&amp;rft.date=1957&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.jstor.org%2Fstable%2F1952449&amp;rft.aulast=Hacker&amp;rft.aufirst=Andrew&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APresbyterianism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Baltzell (1964). <i>The Protestant Establishment</i>. p.&#160;9.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Protestant+Establishment&amp;rft.pages=9&amp;rft.date=1964&amp;rft.au=Baltzell&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APresbyterianism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Atkins2016-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Atkins2016_10-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Atkins2016_10-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Atkins, Gareth (1 August 2016). <i>Making and Remaking Saints in Nineteenth-Century Britain</i>. Manchester University Press. p.&#160;104. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781526100238" title="Special:BookSources/9781526100238">9781526100238</a>. <q>For many Presbyterian evangelicals in Scotland, the \'achievements of the Reformation represented the return to a native or national tradition, the rejection of an alien tyranny that had suppressed ... Scotland\'s true character as a Presbyterian nation enjoying the benefits of civil and religious liberty\'. What they had in mind was the mission established by Columba at Iona and the subsequent spread of Christianity through the Culdees of the seventh to eleventh centuries. For Presbyterian scholars in the nineteenth century, these communities of clergy who differed in organisation and ethos from later monastic orders were further evidence of the similarity between early Christianity in Ireland and Scotland and later Presbyterianism. This interpretation of the character of the Celtic Church was an important aspect of Presbyterian identity in global terms. At the first meeting in 1877 of the Alliance of the Reformed Churches holding the Presbyterian System (later the World Alliance of Reformed Churches), Peter Lorimer (1812\xe2\x80\x9379), a Presbyterian professor in London, noted \'that the early Church of St. Patrick, Columba, and Columbanus, was far more nearly allied in its fundamental principles of order and discipline to the Presbyterian than to the Episcopalian Churches of modern times\'.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Making+and+Remaking+Saints+in+Nineteenth-Century+Britain&amp;rft.pages=104&amp;rft.pub=Manchester+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2016-08-01&amp;rft.isbn=9781526100238&amp;rft.aulast=Atkins&amp;rft.aufirst=Gareth&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APresbyterianism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-TaylorAnderson1852-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-TaylorAnderson1852_11-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Taylor, James; Anderson, John (1852). <i>The Pictorial History of Scotland</i>. p.&#160;51. <q>The zealous Presbyterian maintains, that the church established by Columba was formed on a Presbyterian model, and that it recognized the great principle of clerical equality.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Pictorial+History+of+Scotland&amp;rft.pages=51&amp;rft.date=1852&amp;rft.aulast=Taylor&amp;rft.aufirst=James&amp;rft.au=Anderson%2C+John&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APresbyterianism" class="Z3988"></span> <span class="cs1-visible-error error citation-comment"><code class="cs1-code">&#124;access-date=</code> requires <code class="cs1-code">&#124;url=</code> (<a href="/wiki/Help:CS1_errors#accessdate_missing_url" title="Help:CS1 errors">help</a>)</span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Bradley2013-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Bradley2013_12-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Bradley, Ian (24 July 2013). <i>Columba</i>. (1920). "Apostolicity of Presbyterianism: Ancient Culdeeism and Modern Presbyterianism". <i>The Presbyterian Magazine</i>. <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_(USA)" title="Presbyterian Church (USA)">Presbyterian Church (USA)</a>. <b>26</b> (1\xe2\x80\x937): 529. <q>The Culdees who claimed at the Synod of Whitby apostolic descent from St. John, as against the Romish claim of the authority of St. Peter, retired into Scotland.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Presbyterian+Magazine&amp;rft.atitle=Apostolicity+of+Presbyterianism%3A+Ancient+Culdeeism+and+Modern+Presbyterianism&amp;rft.volume=26&amp;rft.issue=1%E2%80%937&amp;rft.pages=529&amp;rft.date=1920&amp;rft.aulast=Dickens-Lewis&amp;rft.aufirst=W.F.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APresbyterianism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Thomson1896-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Thomson1896_14-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Thomson, Thomas (1896). <i>A History of the Scottish People from the Earliest Times</i>. Blackie. p.&#160;141. <q>...for the primitive apostolic church which St. John had established in the East and Columba transported to our shores. Thus the days of Culdeeism were numbered, and she was now awaiting the martyrs doom.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+History+of+the+Scottish+People+from+the+Earliest+Times&amp;rft.pages=141&amp;rft.pub=Blackie&amp;rft.date=1896&amp;rft.aulast=Thomson&amp;rft.aufirst=Thomas&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APresbyterianism" class="Z3988"></span> <span class="cs1-visible-error error citation-comment"><code class="cs1-code">&#124;access-date=</code> requires <code class="cs1-code">&#124;url=</code> (<a href="/wiki/Help:CS1_errors#accessdate_missing_url" title="Help:CS1 errors">help</a>)</span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Mackay1902-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Mackay1902_15-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Mackay, John; Mackay, Annie Maclean Sharp (1902). <i>The Celtic Monthly</i>. Archibald Sinclair. p.&#160;236.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Celtic+Monthly&amp;rft.pages=236&amp;rft.pub=Archibald+Sinclair&amp;rft.date=1902&amp;rft.aulast=Mackay&amp;rft.aufirst=John&amp;rft.au=Mackay%2C+Annie+Maclean+Sharp&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APresbyterianism" class="Z3988"></span> <span class="cs1-visible-error error citation-comment"><code class="cs1-code">&#124;access-date=</code> requires <code class="cs1-code">&#124;url=</code> (<a href="/wiki/Help:CS1_errors#accessdate_missing_url" title="Help:CS1 errors">help</a>)</span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-HannrachainArmstrong2014-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-HannrachainArmstrong2014_16-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Hannrachain, T. O\'; Armstrong, R.; hAnnrach\xc3\xa1in, Tadhg \xc3\x93 (30 July 2014). <i>Christianities in the Early Modern Celtic World</i>. Springer. p.&#160;198. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781137306357" title="Special:BookSources/9781137306357">9781137306357</a>. <q>Presbyterians after 1690 gave yet more play to \'Culdeeism\', a reading of the past wherein \'culdees\' (derived from c\xc3\xa9li d\xc3\xa9) were presented as upholding a native, collegiate, proto presbyterian church government uncontaminated by bishops.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Christianities+in+the+Early+Modern+Celtic+World&amp;rft.pages=198&amp;rft.pub=Springer&amp;rft.date=2014-07-30&amp;rft.isbn=9781137306357&amp;rft.aulast=Hannrachain&amp;rft.aufirst=T.+O%27&amp;rft.au=Armstrong%2C+R.&amp;rft.au=hAnnrach%C3%A1in%2C+Tadhg+%C3%93&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APresbyterianism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Rankin1884-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Rankin1884_17-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Rankin, James (1884). <i>The Young Churchman: lessons on the Creed, the Commandments, the means of grace, and the Church</i>. William Blackwood and Sons. p.&#160;84. <q>For seven whole centuries (400\xe2\x80\x931100 A.D.) there existed in Scotland a genuine Celtic Church, apparently of Greek origin, and in close connection with both Ireland and Wales. In this Celtic Church no Pope was recognized, and no prelatical of diocesan bishops existed. Their bishops were of the primitive New Testament style\xe2\x80\x94presbyter-bishops. Easter was kept at a different time from that of Rome. The tonsure of the monks was not, like that of Rome, on the crown, but across the forehead from ear to ear. The monastic system of the Celtic Church was extremely simple\xe2\x80\x94small communities of twelve men were presided over by an abbot (kindred to the Patriarch title of the Greeks), who took precedence of the humble parochial bishops.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Young+Churchman%3A+lessons+on+the+Creed%2C+the+Commandments%2C+the+means+of+grace%2C+and+the+Church&amp;rft.pages=84&amp;rft.pub=William+Blackwood+and+Sons&amp;rft.date=1884&amp;rft.aulast=Rankin&amp;rft.aufirst=James&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APresbyterianism" class="Z3988"></span> <span class="cs1-visible-error error citation-comment"><code class="cs1-code">&#124;access-date=</code> requires <code class="cs1-code">&#124;url=</code> (<a href="/wiki/Help:CS1_errors#accessdate_missing_url" title="Help:CS1 errors">help</a>)</span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Skinner1999-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Skinner1999_18-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Skinner1999_18-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Sawyers, June Skinner (1999). <i>Maverick Guide to Scotland</i>. Pelican Publishing. p.&#160;57. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781455608669" title="Special:BookSources/9781455608669">9781455608669</a>. <q>The Celtic Church evolved separated from the Roman Catholic Church. The Celtic Church was primarily monastic, and the monasteries were administered by an abbot. Not as organized as the church in Rome, it was a much looser institution. The Celtic Church celebrated Easter on a different date from the Roman, too. Life within the Celtic Church tended to be ascetic. Education was an important element, as was passion for spreading the word, that is, evangelism. The Celtic brothers led a simple life in simply constructed buildings. The churches and monastic buildings were usually made of wood and wattle and had thatched roofs. After the death of St. Columba in A.D. 597, the autonomy of the Celtic Church did not last long. The Synod of Whitby in 664 decided, once and for all, that Easter would be celebrated according to the Roman date, not the Celtic date. This was the beginning of the end for the Celtic Church.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Maverick+Guide+to+Scotland&amp;rft.pages=57&amp;rft.pub=Pelican+Publishing&amp;rft.date=1999&amp;rft.isbn=9781455608669&amp;rft.aulast=Sawyers&amp;rft.aufirst=June+Skinner&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APresbyterianism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Eggins2015-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Eggins2015_19-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Eggins, Brian (2 March 2015). <i>History &amp; Hope: The Alliance Party in Northern Ireland</i>. History Press. p.&#160;15. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780750964753" title="Special:BookSources/9780750964753">9780750964753</a>. <q>After the Synod of Whitby in about 664, the Roman tradition was imposed on the whole Church, though remnants of the Celtic tradition lingered in practice.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=History+%26+Hope%3A+The+Alliance+Party+in+Northern+Ireland&amp;rft.pages=15&amp;rft.pub=History+Press&amp;rft.date=2015-03-02&amp;rft.isbn=9780750964753&amp;rft.aulast=Eggins&amp;rft.aufirst=Brian&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APresbyterianism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Bowden2005-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Bowden2005_20-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Bowden, John Stephen (2005). <i>Encyclopedia of Christianity</i>. <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University_Press" title="Oxford University Press">Oxford University Press</a>. p.&#160;242}quote=A distinctive part of Scottish Presbyterian worship is the singing of metrical psalms, many of them set to old Celtic Christianity Scottish traditional and folk tunes. These verse psalms have been exported to Africa, North America and other parts of the world where Presbyterian Scots missionaries or Emigres have been influential. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780195223934" title="Special:BookSources/9780195223934">9780195223934</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Encyclopedia+of+Christianity&amp;rft.pages=242%7Dquote%3DA+distinctive+part+of+Scottish+Presbyterian+worship+is+the+singing+of+metrical+psalms%2C+many+of+them+set+to+old+Celtic+Christianity+Scottish+traditional+and+folk+tunes.+These+verse+psalms+have+been+exported+to+Africa%2C+North+America+and+other+parts+of+the+world+where+Presbyterian+Scots+missionaries+or+Emigres+have+been+influential.&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.isbn=9780195223934&amp;rft.aulast=Bowden&amp;rft.aufirst=John+Stephen&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APresbyterianism" class="Z3988"></span> <span class="cs1-visible-error error citation-comment"><code class="cs1-code">&#124;access-date=</code> requires <code class="cs1-code">&#124;url=</code> (<a href="/wiki/Help:CS1_errors#accessdate_missing_url" title="Help:CS1 errors">help</a>)</span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-21">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Hechter, Michael (1995). <i>Internal Colonialism: The Celtic Fringe in British National Development</i>. Transaction Publishers. p.&#160;168. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781412826457" title="Special:BookSources/9781412826457">9781412826457</a>. <q>Last, because Scotland was a sovereign land in the sixteenth century, the Scottish Reformation came under the influence of John Knox rather than Henry Tudor. The organization of the Church of Scotland became Presbyterian, with significant Calvinist influences, rather than Episcopalian. Upon incorporation Scotland was allowed to keep her church intact. These regional religious differences were to an extent superimposed upon linguistic differences in Wales, Scotland, and Ireland. One of the legacies of the Celtic social organization was the persistence of the Celtic languages Gaelic and Welsh among certain groups in the periphery.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Internal+Colonialism%3A+The+Celtic+Fringe+in+British+National+Development&amp;rft.pages=168&amp;rft.pub=Transaction+Publishers&amp;rft.date=1995&amp;rft.isbn=9781412826457&amp;rft.aulast=Hechter&amp;rft.aufirst=Michael&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APresbyterianism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-22">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.newadvent.org/cathen/13627a.htm">"Established Church of Scotland"</a>. <i>Catholic Encyclopedia</i><span class="reference-accessdate">.
